Thin
Lizzy
performing
at
the











<a
href="/wiki/Manchester_Apollo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Manchester
Apollo"
class="mw-redirect">Manchester
Apollo</a>,
showing
their
famous
dual
guitars
on
each
side









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
beginning
of
1982
was
marred
by
both
Downey
and
Gorham
having
to
take
breaks
from
the
European
tour
to
recover
from
personal
problems.
Downey
was
involved
in
a
fight
in
a
nightclub
in
Denmark
in
February,<sup
id="cite_ref-byrne_4-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-byrne-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Gorham
was
suffering
from
drug-induced
exhaustion.<sup
id="cite_ref-bailie_6-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bailie-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
Downey
missed
five
concerts,
and
was
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Nauseef?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Nauseef">Mark
Nauseef</a>
again
for
three
of
them,
and
by
Mike
Mesbur
of
support
band
The
Lookalikes
for
the
other
two.<sup
id="cite_ref-Guide_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guide-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
March,
Gorham
collapsed
and
returned
home;
eight
concerts
were
performed
as
a
quartet
and
six
others
were
postponed.<sup
id="cite_ref-Guide_16-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guide-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Later
in
the
year,
Lynott
went
on
a
solo
tour
and
released
his
second
solo
album,
which
did
not
sell
particularly
well.
Snowy
White
left
the
band
in
August
1982,
having
tired
of
the
disorganised
schedules
and
Lynott's
drug
problems,
although
by
his
own
admission
he
was
too
restrained
and
quiet
to
fit
in
well
with
his
more
raucous
bandmates.<sup
id="cite_ref-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
White
went
on
to
achieve
top
ten
chart
success
in
the
UK
with
his
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bird_of_Paradise_(Snowy_White_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bird
of
Paradise
(Snowy
White
song)">Bird
of
Paradise</a>&quot;
in
1983.
Long-time
co-manager
Chris
O'Donnell
also
left
at
this
time,
later
stating,
&quot;A
once-brilliant
band
was
turning
to
crap
before
my
very
eyes.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Lynott
wanted
to
find
a
replacement
for
White
before
starting
to
record
the
next
album,
which
would
turn
out
to
be
the
band's
last.
By
September
1982,
he
had
settled
on
<a
href="/wiki/John_Sykes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Sykes">John
Sykes</a>
who
had
been
a
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/Tygers_of_Pan_Tang?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tygers
of
Pan
Tang">Tygers
of
Pan
Tang</a>,
and
he
co-wrote
the
first
single
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cold_Sweat_(Thin_Lizzy_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cold
Sweat
(Thin
Lizzy
song)">Cold
Sweat</a>&quot;,
although
the
rest
of
the
album
had
already
been
written.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Thunder_and_Lightning_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Thunder
and
Lightning
(album)">Thunder
and
Lightning</a></i>
was
released
in
March
1983,
and
was
much
more
successful
than
its
predecessor,
reaching
no.
4
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-brooks_7-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brooks-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
Sykes'
presence
had
rejuvenated
the
band
musically,
the
composing
credits
were
evenly
shared,
and
the
style
had
grown
much
heavier,
veering
towards
<a
href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heavy
metal
music">heavy
metal</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-byrne_4-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-byrne-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
tour
to
support
the
album
was
to
be
a
farewell
tour,
although
Lynott
was
not
convinced
that
this
would
be
the
end
of
the
band.
Sykes
wanted
to
continue,
although
Gorham
had
had
enough.<sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
was
successful,
and
some
concerts
were
recorded
to
compile
a
live
album.
Partway
into
the
tour,
many
of
Thin
Lizzy's
past
guitarists
were
invited
onstage
to
contribute
to
some
of
the
songs
they
had
originally
recorded,
the
only
exception
being
Snowy
White.
The
album
was
released
in
October
1983
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Life_(Thin_Lizzy_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Life
(Thin
Lizzy
album)">Life</a></i>,
which
included
an
older
performance
of
&quot;Renegade&quot;
featuring
White,
and
reached
no.
29
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-brooks_7-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brooks-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
continued
while
two
more
singles
were
released,
the
last
of
them,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Sun_Goes_Down_(Thin_Lizzy_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Sun
Goes
Down
(Thin
Lizzy
song)">The
Sun
Goes
Down</a>&quot;,
only
reaching
no.
52
in
August.
Lynott
also
undertook
another
solo
tour,
accompanied
by
Downey
and
Sykes,
under
the
name
of
The
Three
Musketeers.<sup
id="cite_ref-byrne_4-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-byrne-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>After
a
difficult
leg
of
the
tour
in
Japan,
where
some
members
of
the
band
had
difficulty
obtaining
heroin,<sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Thin
Lizzy
played
their
final
UK
concert
before
their
break-up
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
Festival"
class="mw-redirect">Reading
Festival</a>
on
28
August
1983,
which
was
eventually
released
in
1992
as
their
<i><a
href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_One_Live_in_Concert_(Thin_Lizzy_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BBC
Radio
One
Live
in
Concert
(Thin
Lizzy
album)">BBC
Radio
One
Live
in
Concert</a></i>
album.
The
last
concert
came
in
<a
href="/wiki/Nuremberg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nuremberg">Nuremberg</a>
on
4
September,
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Monsters_of_Rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monsters
of
Rock">Monsters
of
Rock</a>
festival,
after
which
the
band
members
went
their
separate
ways.<sup
id="cite_ref-brooks_7-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brooks-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Post-Thin_Lizzy_projects_and_tributes_.281985.E2.80.9396.29">Post-Thin
Lizzy
projects
and
tributes
(1985–96)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Thin_Lizzy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Post-Thin
Lizzy
projects
and
tributes
(1985–96)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Before
the
end
of
1983,
Phil
Lynott
formed
a
new
band
called
<a
href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grand
Slam
(band)">Grand
Slam</a>,
but
they
were
never
able
to
secure
a
contract
with
a
record
company
and
split
by
the
beginning
of
1985.<sup
id="cite_ref-bailie_6-13"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bailie-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
Sykes
and
Downey
initially
agreed
to
be
a
part
of
the
band,
but
Sykes
joined
<a
href="/wiki/Whitesnake?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Whitesnake">Whitesnake</a>
and
Downey
also
changed
his
mind.
Lynott
began
to
focus
more
on
his
solo
career
and
enjoyed
a
no.
5
hit
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Out_in_the_Fields_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Out
in
the
Fields
(song)">Out
in
the
Fields</a>&quot;
with
Gary
Moore
in
May
1985.<sup
id="cite_ref-bailie_6-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bailie-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song,
composed
by
Moore,
was
taken
from
his
solo
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Run_for_Cover_(Gary_Moore_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Run
for
Cover
(Gary
Moore
album)">Run
for
Cover</a></i>
featuring
various
contributions
from
Lynott.
Lynott's
solo
efforts
did
not
fare
so
well,
and
his
last
single,
&quot;Nineteen&quot;,
only
reached
no.
76
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-black_rose_18-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-black_rose-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Before
his
death,
Lynott
was
planning
a
third
solo
album,
and
had
spoken
to
Downey
about
a
possible
reformation
of
Thin
Lizzy
around
March
1986,
with
Gorham
and
Sykes,
and
had
booked
studio
time
for
January
of
that
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
he
died
in
hospital
in
<a
href="/wiki/Salisbury?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Salisbury">Salisbury</a>,
Wiltshire,
on
4
January
1986,
aged
36,
having
suffered
from
internal
<a
href="/wiki/Abscess?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Abscess">abscesses</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Pneumonia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Sepsis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sepsis">septicaemia</a>,
brought
on
by
his
drug
dependency,
which
led
to
multiple
organ
failure.<sup
id="cite_ref-byrne_4-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-byrne-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-brooks_7-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brooks-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
17
May,
Thin
Lizzy
reformed
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Self_Aid?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Self
Aid">Self
Aid</a>
concert,
with
a
line-up
of
Gary
Moore,
Downey,
Gorham,
Wharton
and
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Daisley?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Daisley">Bob
Daisley</a>
on
bass.
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Geldof?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Geldof">Bob
Geldof</a>
and
Moore
handled
most
lead
vocals,
though
various
singers
got
onstage
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Whiskey_in_the_Jar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Whiskey
in
the
Jar">Whiskey
in
the
Jar</a>&quot;.
A
compilation
album,
<i>Soldier
of
Fortune</i>,
was
released
in
1987,
and
also
that
year,
the
&quot;Vibe
for
Philo&quot;
tribute
concert
in
Lynott's
memory
was
organised
by
Dublin
DJ
and
promoter
Smiley
Bolger,
which
continues
on
an
annual
basis
on
the
anniversary
of
Lynott's
death.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg/220px-Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg"
width="220"
height="159"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg/330px-Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg/440px-Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brian_Robertson_in_2011.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Brian
Robertson
performing
at
the
25th
annual
&quot;Vibe
for
Philo&quot;
on
4
January
2011









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
remaining
members
of
Thin
Lizzy
did
not
work
together
until
the
recording
of
the
single
&quot;Dedication&quot;
in
October
1990,
when
a
rough
demo
of
Lynott's
was
worked
into
a
finished
song
to
commemorate
the
fifth
anniversary
of
his
death.
The
song
dated
from
the
Grand
Slam
days
and
had
been
originally
written
with
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Laurence_Archer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Laurence
Archer">Laurence
Archer</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-byrne_4-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-byrne-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Modern
recording
techniques
were
used
to
replace
the
guitar
and
drum
tracks
with
new
work
by
Downey
and
Gorham.
Gary
Moore
had
agreed
to
participate
as
well,
but
ultimately
did
not
do
so.<sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
charted
in
the
UK
at
no.
35
during
early
1991,
and
no.
2
in
Ireland,<sup
id="cite_ref-irishchart_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-irishchart-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
featured
on
another
greatest
hits
compilation
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dedication:_The_Very_Best_of_Thin_Lizzy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dedication:
The
Very
Best
of
Thin
Lizzy">Dedication:
The
Very
Best
of
Thin
Lizzy</a></i>,
released
in
February
of
that
year,
which
reached
no.
8
in
the
UK
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-bailie_6-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bailie-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
a
follow-up
reissue
of
&quot;The
Boys
Are
Back
in
Town&quot;
only
reached
no.
63
in
the
UK,<sup
id="cite_ref-UK_11-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-UK-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
although
it
peaked
at
no.
16
in
Ireland.<sup
id="cite_ref-irishchart_21-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-irishchart-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Following
this,
numerous
small
reunion
projects
began
to
appear.
In
1991,
a
line-up
featuring
Robertson
and
Downey
performed
with
<a
href="/wiki/Bobby_Tench?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bobby
Tench">Bobby
Tench</a>
on
lead
vocals,
ex-Grand
Slam
member
Doish
Nagle
on
guitar
and
Doug
Brockie
on
bass.
They
toured
Ireland
briefly
with
a
series
of
&quot;An
Evening
of
Thin
Lizzy&quot;
concerts.<sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
August
1994,
Downey,
Bell,
Robertson
and
Wharton
held
a
tribute
concert
in
<a
href="/wiki/Wolverhampton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wolverhampton">Wolverhampton</a>,
together
with
tribute
bands
Limehouse
Lizzy,
Ain't
Lizzy
and
Bad
Habitz.<sup
id="cite_ref-bailie_6-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bailie-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
Another
version
of
Thin
Lizzy
was
formed
later
that
year
by
John
Sykes
(now
also
performing
lead
vocals)
with
Downey,
Gorham
and
Wharton,
and
with
bass
parts
played
by
<a
href="/wiki/Marco_Mendoza?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marco
Mendoza">Marco
Mendoza</a>,
who
had
played
with
Sykes
in
<a
href="/wiki/Blue_Murder_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blue
Murder
(band)">Blue
Murder</a>
from
1991–93.
The
tour
was
advertised
as
a
tribute
to
Phil
Lynott.<sup
id="cite_ref-byrne_4-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-byrne-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
This
line-up
also
played
at
the
Vibe
for
Philo
gig
on
4
January
1996,
with
a
number
of
other
notable
musicians
including
Eric
Bell,
Midge
Ure,
<a
href="/wiki/Henry_Rollins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Henry
Rollins">Henry
Rollins</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Therapy%3F?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Therapy?">Therapy?</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Elliott?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Elliott">Joe
Elliott</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rick_Savage?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rick
Savage">Rick
Savage</a>
from
<a
href="/wiki/Def_Leppard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Def
Leppard">Def
Leppard</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-bailie_6-17"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bailie-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1994,
a
collection
of
Thin
Lizzy
tracks
from
the
BBC
Radio
1
<a
href="/wiki/The_Peel_Sessions_(Thin_Lizzy_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Peel
Sessions
(Thin
Lizzy
album)">Peel
Sessions</a>
was
released,
and
yet
another
compilation
album
was
brought
out
in
1996,
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wild_One:_The_Very_Best_Of_Thin_Lizzy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wild
One:
The
Very
Best
Of
Thin
Lizzy"
class="mw-redirect">Wild
One:
The
Very
Best
Of
Thin
Lizzy</a></i>.
This
was
successful,
although
strangely
it
did
not
feature
the
title
track,
&quot;Wild
One&quot;.</p>








<p>On
20
August
1996,
<a
href="/wiki/Rude_Awakening_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rude
Awakening
(band)">Rude
Awakening</a>
bassist
Robert
Ryder
held
&quot;A
Celebration
of
the
Life
of
Philip
Lynott&quot;
at
<a
href="/wiki/Avalon_Hollywood?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Avalon
Hollywood">the
Palace
in
Hollywood,
California</a>
at
the
request
of
Lynott's
mother,
Philomena,
to
commemorate
both
Phil
Lynott's
birthday
and
the
tenth
year
of
his
passing.
Philomena
Lynott,
her
partner
Dennis
Keeley,
and
Smiley
Bolger
(Ireland's
Vibe
For
Philo
promoter)
were
flown
to
Los
Angeles
by
Ryder
to
make
a
personal
appearance
at
the
show.
It
featured
concert
performances
by
Rude
Awakening,
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Sheehan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Sheehan">Billy
Sheehan</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rudy_Sarzo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rudy
Sarzo">Rudy
Sarzo</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Norum?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Norum">John
Norum</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Carmine_Appice?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Carmine
Appice">Carmine
Appice</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Phantom_Blue?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phantom
Blue">Phantom
Blue</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Soma?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Soma">Soma</a>,
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Roy_Z?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roy
Z">Roy
Z</a>
and
his
band
the
Tribe
of
Gypsies,
Mark
Ferrari,
Oslo,
<a
href="/wiki/Bang_Tango?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bang
Tango">Bang
Tango</a>,
Stash,
Iron
Cross
and
Irish
singer-songwriter
Mark
Dignam.</p>

class="mw-headline"

Lizzy
without
Lynott
(1996–present)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Thin_Lizzy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Thin
Lizzy
without
Lynott
(1996–present)">edit</a>]</span></h3>

The
reformed
version
of
Thin
Lizzy
at











<a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gods
of
Metal">Gods
of
Metal</a>,
2007









</div>

<p>In
1996
John
Sykes
decided
to
reactivate
Thin
Lizzy,
presenting
the
band
as
a
tribute
to
Phil
Lynott's
life
and
work.<sup
id="cite_ref-sykes99_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sykes99-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
decided
to
take
on
the
role
of
lead
vocals
himself
in
the
absence
of
Lynott,
and
persuaded
Scott
Gorham,
Brian
Downey
and
Darren
Wharton
to
return
to
the
fold.
To
complete
the
line-up,
Marco
Mendoza
continued
in
Lynott's
role
as
bass
player.
They
received
criticism
for
using
the
Thin
Lizzy
name
without
Lynott
being
present,<sup
id="cite_ref-byrne_4-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-byrne-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
but
the
band
only
played
hits
from
Thin
Lizzy's
back
catalogue,
and
did
not
compose
any
new
material.<sup
id="cite_ref-sykes99_22-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sykes99-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
1997,
<a
href="/wiki/Tommy_Aldridge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tommy
Aldridge">Tommy
Aldridge</a>
filled
in
on
drums
when
Brian
Downey
was
unable
to,
and
became
a
full
member
when
Downey
left
shortly
thereafter.
This
line-up
remained
stable
through
to
2000,
when
the
group
recorded
a
live
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_Night_Only_(Thin_Lizzy_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Night
Only
(Thin
Lizzy
album)">One
Night
Only</a></i>.
The
band
went
on
to
tour
the
US
playing
clubs
in
early
2001,
but
Wharton
had
already
left
the
band
by
the
time
of
the
tour.
From
2000
to
2003,
Mendoza
toured
with
<a
href="/wiki/Ted_Nugent?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ted
Nugent">Ted
Nugent</a>,
and
with
<a
href="/wiki/Whitesnake?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Whitesnake">Whitesnake</a>
in
2004.
Sykes
released
two
solo
albums
in
the
gap
in
between
2002–03,
while
Gorham
worked
with
his
band
<a
href="/wiki/21_Guns_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="21
Guns
(band)">21
Guns</a>.</p>








<p>Wharton
later
stated
that
Thin
Lizzy
would
have
been
better
suited
to
playing
fewer
concerts,
in
bigger
venues.
He
also
felt
that
after
the
experience
of
fronting
his
own
band
<a
href="/wiki/Dare_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dare
(band)">Dare</a>,
it
was
not
satisfying
enough
to
play
keyboards
behind
Gorham
and
Sykes.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
Sykes
said
that
all
the
previous
Thin
Lizzy
members
were
welcome
to
play
with
Thin
Lizzy
at
any
time.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2004,
Thin
Lizzy
worked
together
again,
with
Sykes
and
Gorham
bringing
in
ex-<a
href="/wiki/Angel_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Angel
(band)">Angel</a>
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Randy_Gregg_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Randy
Gregg
(musician)">Randy
Gregg</a>,
and
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Lee_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Lee
(musician)">Michael
Lee</a>,
who
had
played
with
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_Plant?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Robert
Plant">Robert
Plant</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Cult?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Cult">The
Cult</a>
among
others.
They
toured
in
North
America
in
both
the
winter
and
then
the
summer
as
special
guests
of
Deep
Purple.
This
line-up
proved
temporary
however,
with
Mendoza
returning
in
2005,
and
Aldridge
returning
in
2007.
There
were
no
plans
for
a
new
album
though
Thin
Lizzy
continued
to
tour.
At
the
London
<a
href="/wiki/Hammersmith_Apollo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hammersmith
Apollo">Hammersmith
Apollo</a>
concert
of
13
December
2007,
the
line-up
was
Sykes,
Gorham,
Aldridge
and
<a
href="/wiki/Francesco_DiCosmo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Francesco
DiCosmo">Francesco
DiCosmo</a>
on
bass.<sup
id="cite_ref-Thin_Lizzy_official_website_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Thin_Lizzy_official_website-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Sykes
stated
that
Thin
Lizzy
was
now
&quot;more
of
a
tribute
thing&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-sykes99_22-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sykes99-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
that
it
would
be
wrong
to
record
new
material
under
that
name.
He
added
that
while
the
existing
band
members
might
record
together,
it
would
not
be
as
Thin
Lizzy.<sup
id="cite_ref-sykes99_22-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sykes99-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2007,
Gorham
said
that
Lynott
still
received
the
biggest
cheer
of
the
night
at
concerts,
and
that
the
current
Thin
Lizzy
was
not
active
simply
for
money.<sup
id="cite_ref-gorham_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gorham-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;We'd
stop
if
we
thought
we
were
just
going
through
the
motions...
I
think
that
has
a
lot
to
do
with
the
songs
–
if
they
were
inferior,
then
maybe
we
would
have
got
tired
of
it
all.
But
they're
not
and
we
haven't,&quot;
he
said.<sup
id="cite_ref-gorham_26-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gorham-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
January
2011,
Gorham
maintained
that
Lynott
would
have
approved
of
the
continuation
of
the
band:
&quot;He
worked
long
hours
and
travelled
thousands
of
miles
to
get
it
to
a
certain
level.
There's
no
way
he
would
have
said
'No-one
should
play
those
songs
again.'&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>It
had
been
announced
that
Thin
Lizzy,
along
with
The
Answer,
were
to
support
<a
href="/wiki/AC/DC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a>
at
stadium
shows
in
England,
Ireland
and
Scotland
at
the
end
of
June
2009,
but
these
appearances
were
cancelled
after
drummer
Aldridge
broke
his
collarbone
in
an
accident.
On
30
June,
the
band's
website
announced
that
Sykes
had
left
Thin
Lizzy
and
all
shows
for
the
rest
of
2009
were
cancelled
or
postponed.
Gorham
stated
that
he
would
announce
Thin
Lizzy's
future
plans
shortly.
In
a
statement,
he
said,
&quot;It's
been
a
very
tough
time
of
late
for
myself
and
the
band,
firstly
with
drummer
Tommy
Aldridge's
injury
and
now
the
subsequent
decision
for
John
and
the
rest
of
the
group
to
go
their
separate
ways.
I
can
only
apologise
to
everyone
who
has
supported
us
over
the
years,
but
we
will
be
back
up
to
full
speed
soon.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Thin_Lizzy_official_website_25-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Thin_Lizzy_official_website-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
September
2009,
Gorham
began
to
assemble
a
new
version
of
Thin
Lizzy,
and
in
May
2010
a
new
line-up
was
announced.
Joining
Gorham
was
original
drummer
Brian
Downey,
long-standing
keyboardist
Darren
Wharton,
<a
href="/wiki/Def_Leppard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Def
Leppard">Def
Leppard</a>
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Vivian_Campbell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vivian
Campbell">Vivian
Campbell</a>,
and
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Ricky_Warwick?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ricky
Warwick">Ricky
Warwick</a>
from
<a
href="/wiki/The_Almighty_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Almighty
(band)">The
Almighty</a>,
while
Marco
Mendoza
returned
to
fill
the
bass
guitar
role.
Ex-Lizzy
guitarist
Brian
Robertson
was
asked
if
he
wanted
to
participate
but
had
previous
commitments
to
his
own
solo
career.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
addition
to
a
full
UK
and
European
tour
beginning
in
January
2011,
the
band
initially
announced
a
concert
for
4
January
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/The_O2_(Dublin)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
O2
(Dublin)">O2
Arena</a>
in
Dublin,
which
was
in
conflict
with
the
2011
&quot;Vibe
for
Philo&quot;.
The
tour
itself
started
on
6
January
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Music_Hall_Aberdeen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
Hall
Aberdeen">Music
Hall
Aberdeen</a>
in
the
UK,
with
the
band
finishing
the
tour
in
The
Olympia,
Dublin
on
17
February
2011,
having
cancelled
the
O2
show.<sup
id="cite_ref-29"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>It
was
announced
in
April
2011
that
Vivian
Campbell
would
have
to
leave
Thin
Lizzy
to
rejoin
Def
Leppard
after
one
final
gig
on
28
May.
He
was
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Guns_N%27_Roses?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Guns
N'
Roses">Guns
N'
Roses</a>
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Richard_Fortus?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richard
Fortus">Richard
Fortus</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
28
August,
it
was
announced
that
<a
href="/wiki/Damon_Johnson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Damon
Johnson">Damon
Johnson</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Alice_Cooper?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alice
Cooper">Alice
Cooper</a>'s
band
would
be
replacing
Fortus
for
Thin
Lizzy's
tour
of
the
US
with
<a
href="/wiki/Judas_Priest?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Judas
Priest">Judas
Priest</a>.
Fortus
returned
to
tour
with
Guns
N'
Roses
for
the
rest
of
the
year,
and
Johnson
has
since
replaced
Fortus
permanently.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<i>(foreground)</i>

<p>In
March
2011,
Gorham
told
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard.com</a>
that
Thin
Lizzy
may
record
a
new
album
in
the
future,
saying,
&quot;That's
the
No.&nbsp;1
question
we're
getting
from
people
–
are
we
gonna
record
some
new
material?
The
fans
seem
to
trust
this
line-up,
and
I
don't
blame
them.
We've
kind
of
jumped
this
emotional
hurdle
together.
Ricky's
writing
some
fucking
killer
lyrics,
and
with
the
kind
of
talent
that's
in
Thin
Lizzy
now
I
think
we
can
pull
off
a
really
cool
set
of
tunes.
At
least
it's
something
that
we
can
think
about
now,
where
before
it
wasn't
on
the
table.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
25
June
2012,
Thin
Lizzy
were
in
the
studio
recording
new
material,
although
it
was
not
clear
how
many
songs
would
be
recorded
or
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-33"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
10
October
2012,
Thin
Lizzy
announced
that
the
new
material
would
not
be
released
under
the
Thin
Lizzy
name,
but
would
be
released
under
a
different
name
in
due
course.
According
to
Gorham,
this
was
&quot;out
of
respect
to
Phil
Lynott
and
the
legacy
he
created&quot;,
though
he
confirmed
that
the
new
material
would
feature
the
classic
Thin
Lizzy
sound.<sup
id="cite_ref-farewell_34-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-farewell-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
Ricky
Warwick
announced
that
the
group
would
cease
regular
touring
as
Thin
Lizzy
at
the
end
of
2012,
but
that
this
did
not
necessarily
mean
they
would
never
play
as
Thin
Lizzy
again.<sup
id="cite_ref-farewell_34-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-farewell-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
20
December
2012,
Gorham
announced
that
the
new
material
would
be
recorded
under
the
name
of
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Star_Riders?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Black
Star
Riders">Black
Star
Riders</a>,
and
that
Downey
and
Wharton
had
chosen
not
to
participate
in
the
new
band
project.
Downey
has
decided
to
take
a
break
from
touring,
and
Wharton
will
be
working
on
his
own
band
<a
href="/wiki/Dare_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dare
(band)">Dare</a>,
and
a
film
project.
It
was
also
announced
that
in
March
2013,
the
band
would
tour
Australia
under
the
Thin
Lizzy
name,
with
Downey
and
Wharton,
as
the
opening
act
on
a
triple
bill
with
<a
href="/wiki/M%C3%B6tley_Cr%C3%BCe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e">M&ouml;tley
Cr&uuml;e</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Kiss_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kiss
(band)">Kiss</a>.
Gorham
stressed
that
Thin
Lizzy
would
still
perform
together
occasionally:
&quot;We'll
still
go
out
as
Thin
Lizzy.
There
are
still
certain
big
festivals
that
we
will
do.
Thin
Lizzy
is
still
on
the
horizon,
we
will
still
go
out
and
do
that
but
in
the
meantime
we
have
Black
Star
Riders
that
we
are
going
to
concentrate
on
also.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Other_Thin_Lizzy_releases_and_tributes">Other
Thin
Lizzy
releases
and
tributes</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Thin_Lizzy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Other
Thin
Lizzy
releases
and
tributes">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>A
boxed
set
of
four
CDs
of
Thin
Lizzy
material
was
released
in
December
2001
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Vagabonds,_Kings,_Warriors,_Angels?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vagabonds,
Kings,
Warriors,
Angels">Vagabonds,
Kings,
Warriors,
Angels</a></i>.
It
contained
all
of
the
band's
major
hits,
and
included
some
rare
songs,
such
as
the
first
single
&quot;The
Farmer&quot;,
and
single
B-sides.<sup
id="cite_ref-36"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
2004
and
2006,
two
further
greatest
hits
compilations
were
released,
with
2004's
double
CD
<i><a
href="/wiki/Thin_Lizzy_Greatest_Hits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Thin
Lizzy
Greatest
Hits"
class="mw-redirect">Greatest
Hits</a></i>
climbing
all
the
way
to
No.&nbsp;3
in
the
UK
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
19
August
2005,
Gary
Moore
staged
a
concert
at
the
Point
Theatre,
Dublin,
promoted
as
&quot;The
Boy
Is
Back
in
Town&quot;.
The
concert
was
staged
to
mark
the
unveiling
of
a
bronze
statue
of
Lynott
on
Dublin's
Harry
Street
in
the
city
centre.
The
performance
also
featured
Brian
Downey,
Eric
Bell,
Brian
Robertson
and
Scott
Gorham.
A
DVD
of
the
concert
was
released
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_Night_in_Dublin:_A_Tribute_to_Phil_Lynott?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Night
in
Dublin:
A
Tribute
to
Phil
Lynott">One
Night
in
Dublin:
A
Tribute
to
Phil
Lynott</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
8
September
2008,
a
15-track
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/UK_Tour_%2775?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Tour
'75">UK
Tour
'75</a></i>
was
released
featuring
the
band
performing
at
Derby
College
on
21
November
1975.
The
album
includes
a
20-page
booklet
of
previously-unseen
photos,
liner
notes
written
by
Brian
Downey
and
extra
material
of
the
band
jamming
during
their
soundcheck.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
March
2009,
VH1
Classic
Records
issued
the
band-authorised
<i><a
href="/wiki/Still_Dangerous?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Still
Dangerous">Still
Dangerous:
Live
At
The
Tower
Theatre
Philadelphia,
1977</a></i>,
a
live
CD
recorded
on
the
Bad
Reputation
tour.
It
was
produced
by
Gorham
and
Glyn
Johns,
and
Johns
also
mixed
the
record.
It
reached
No.&nbsp;98
in
the
UK
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup>
Gorham
has
suggested
there
will
be
further
archival
releases
in
the
future.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
24
January
2011,
Universal
Music
issued
remastered
and
expanded
editions
of
<i>Jailbreak</i>,
<i>Johnny
the
Fox</i>
and
<i>Live
and
Dangerous</i>.
<i>Jailbreak</i>
and
<i>Johnny
the
Fox</i>
are
double
CD
editions
with
the
second
disc
containing
outtakes,
BBC
session
recordings
and
newly
remixed
versions
of
two
of
that
particular
album's
tracks.
<i>Live
and
Dangerous</i>
also
comes
as
a
double
CD
set,
with
two
bonus
tracks
which
are
both
unused
live
recordings.
Previous
CD
editions
of
<i>Live
and
Dangerous</i>
were
single
discs.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Universal
followed
this
with
remasters
of
<i>Bad
Reputation</i>,
<i>Black
Rose</i>
and
<i>Chinatown</i>,
and
in
early
2012,
<i>Nightlife</i>
and
<i>Fighting</i>.
Finally,
<i>Renegade</i>
and
<i>Thunder
and
Lightning</i>
were
remastered
and
re-released
in
2013.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Origin_of_the_band_name">Origin
of
the
band
name</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Thin_Lizzy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
Origin
of
the
band
name">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>The
band's
original
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Eric_Bell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Bell">Eric
Bell</a>,
who
was
a
fan
of
<a
href="/wiki/John_Mayall_%26_the_Bluesbreakers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers">John
Mayall
&amp;
the
Bluesbreakers</a>,
bought
a
copy
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Dandy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Dandy">The
Dandy</a></i>
comic<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
after
seeing
<a
href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Eric
Clapton">Eric
Clapton</a>
depicted
reading
a
copy
of
its
sister
publication
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beano?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beano">The
Beano</a></i>
on
the
cover
of
the
1966
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bluesbreakers_with_Eric_Clapton?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bluesbreakers
with
Eric
Clapton"
class="mw-redirect">Bluesbreakers
with
Eric
Clapton</a></i>.
He
suggested
Tin
Lizzie,
the
name
of
a
robot
character
from
the
comic,
itself
named
for
the
common
nickname
for
the
iconic
<a
href="/wiki/Ford_Model_T?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ford
Model
T">Ford
Model
T</a>
car.
Bell
also
suggested
they
change
'Tin'
to
'Thin'
to
play
on
the
Irish
accent's
propensity
to
drop
the
'h'.
After
a
while,
Lynott
and
Downey
agreed
to
the
idea
and
the
name
stuck,
as
they
thought
the
confusion
was
amusing
and
would
create
a
talking
point.<sup
id="cite_ref-putterford_5-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-putterford-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bailie_6-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bailie-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
some
of
their
early
gigs,
the
band
were
mistakenly
promoted
as
&quot;Tin
Lizzy&quot;
or
&quot;Tin
Lizzie&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-brooks_7-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brooks-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
<span
id="personnel"></span></p>








<h2><span
id="personnel"><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Style_and_legacy">Style
and
legacy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Thin_Lizzy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Style
and
legacy">edit</a>]</span></span></h2>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg/220px-Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg"
width="220"
height="156"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg/330px-Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg/440px-Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Thin_Lizzy_1978-Live_and_Dangerous_lineup.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
The
classic
line-up
showing
the
band's
famous
&quot;twin
guitar&quot;
sound.
L
to
R:
Brian
Robertson
(guitar),
Phil
Lynott
(bass
guitar),
and
Scott
Gorham
(guitar)









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>From
1974,
Thin
Lizzy
switched
from
using
one
lead
guitarist
to
two.
Though
others
had
earlier
used
similar
techniques,
Thin
Lizzy
are
widely
recognised
as
one
of
the
first
hard
rock
bands
to
employ
double
lead
guitar
harmony
sound
–
a
technique
pioneered
by
<a
href="/wiki/Peter_Green%27s_Fleetwood_Mac?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Peter
Green's
Fleetwood
Mac"
class="mw-redirect">Peter
Green's
Fleetwood
Mac</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Wishbone_Ash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wishbone
Ash">Wishbone
Ash</a>
in
the
UK,
whilst
independently
in
the
USA
by
<a
href="/wiki/Lynyrd_Skynyrd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lynyrd
Skynyrd">Lynyrd
Skynyrd</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Allman_Brothers_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Allman
Brothers
Band">The
Allman
Brothers
Band</a>.
This
style
was
later
refined
and
popularised
in
the
mid-1970s
by
bands
like
Thin
Lizzy
and
<a
href="/wiki/Judas_Priest?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Judas
Priest">Judas
Priest</a>,
and
later
by
the
emerging
<a
href="/wiki/New_Wave_of_British_Heavy_Metal?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Wave
of
British
Heavy
Metal">New
Wave
of
British
Heavy
Metal</a>
groups
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Iron_Maiden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Iron
Maiden">Iron
Maiden</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Def_Leppard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Def
Leppard">Def
Leppard</a>.
Iron
Maiden
covered
the
song
&quot;Massacre&quot;
from
Thin
Lizzy's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Johnny_the_Fox?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Johnny
the
Fox">Johnny
the
Fox</a></i>
album,
and
released
it
on
their
1988
single
<a
href="/wiki/Can_I_Play_with_Madness?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Can
I
Play
with
Madness">Can
I
Play
with
Madness</a>.
A
cover
of
&quot;Cowboy
Song&quot;
appears
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Sound_of_White_Noise?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sound
of
White
Noise">Sound
of
White
Noise</a>&quot;
by
<a
href="/wiki/Anthrax_(American_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Anthrax
(American
band)">Anthrax</a>
as
the
bonus
track
for
album's
Japanese
release.</p>








<p>Thin
Lizzy
is
also
the
major
inspiration
for
modern
heavy
metal
bands,
most
notably
<a
href="/wiki/Metallica?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Metallica">Metallica</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Alice_in_Chains?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alice
in
Chains">Alice
in
Chains</a><sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Mastodon_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mastodon
(band)">Mastodon</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Kies_46-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Kies-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
Mastodon
covered
Thin
Lizzy's
classic
&quot;Emerald&quot;,
which
has
been
included
as
a
bonus
track
for
their
Japanese
release
of
their
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Remission_(Mastodon_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Remission
(Mastodon
album)">Remission</a></i>.
They
have
played
the
song
live
several
times,
including
an
acoustic
version
with
Scott
Gorham
on
guitar.<sup
id="cite_ref-Kies_46-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Kies-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Henry_Rollins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Henry
Rollins">Henry
Rollins</a>
has
expressed
a
fondness
for
Thin
Lizzy,<sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rollins_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rollins
Band">Rollins
Band</a>
covered
their
song
&quot;Are
You
Ready?&quot;
on
their
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Get_Some_Go_Again?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Get
Some
Go
Again">Get
Some
Go
Again</a></i>
(2000).
The
2005
release
from
<a
href="/wiki/The_Great_Divide_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Great
Divide
(band)">The
Great
Divide</a>
included
a
cover
of
&quot;Cowboy
Song&quot;
in
two
parts.
<a
href="/wiki/Megadeth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Megadeth">Megadeth</a>
covered
Thin
Lizzy's
”Cold
Sweat”
on
their
2013
release,
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Collider_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Super
Collider
(album)">Super
Collider</a>.</p>

Former

<li><a

onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phil
Lynott">Phil
Lynott</a>
–
bass
guitar,
lead

<script
type="text/javascript">




render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Thin_Lizzy&page=1&ac=24&qid=C90105FE568CCDC43E6152F6E7AB1F8C&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

</script>
